Jamison Brereton

19 (460)
Indra
Bharadv─Бja B─Бrhaspatya
13 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
Like the previous hymn, this one exults in the mighty powers of Indra and in the rich lexicon that describes them, although it is perhaps somewhat less insistent (but see vs. 6ab). Also as in VI.18 the poet exhorts Indra to put his powers to good use for the men associated with the poet. The three middle verses (6тАУ8) all contain the phrase тАЬbring here to us,тАЭ each with a different abstract power as object, and the remaining verses continue these requests for aid and support, especially in defeating enemies and rivals.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra This hymn is something of a bricolage, with numerous phrases, p─Бdas, and whole verses borrowed from elsewhere. (I say тАЬborrowedтАЭ rather than the more neutral тАЬparallel to,тАЭ because the sheer number of the matches strongly suggests that there is a magpie quality to the construction of this hymn. For details of the matches, see GeldnerтАЩs nn. (though he doesnтАЩt note all of them) and Bloomfield Rig-Veda Repetitions

рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪ - рдХрд░реНрддреГрднрд┐рдГ рдкрд░рд┐рдЪрд░рджреНрднрд┐рдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рд░реН рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдиреИрд░реН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдЙрд░реБрд░реНрд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреАрд░реНрдгреЛ рдмрд▓реЗрди, рдкреГрдереБрдГ рдкреНрд░рдерд┐рддрд╕реН рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рдпрд╢рд╕рд╛, рд╕реБрдХреГрддрдГ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБрдХреГрддрдГ рд╡рд╢реАрдХреГрддрд╢реНрдЪ, рднреВрддреН рднрд╡рддреБ ред рднрд╡рддреЗрд░реНрд▓реБрдЩрд┐ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╡рдЪреНрдЫрдкреЛ рд▓реБрдХреН, ‘рднреВрд╕реБрд╡реЛрд╕реНрддрд┐рдЩрд┐’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЧреБрдгрд╛рднрд╛рд╡рдГ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ - рдХрд░реНрддреГрднрд┐рд░рд╕реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ рд╕реБрдХреГрддрд╕реНрд╕рдореНрдпрдХреНрдХреГрддреЛрдпрдореБрд░реБрдГ рдкреГрдереБрд╢реНрдЪ рднрд╡рддреБ ред ‘рд╕реБрдГ рдкреВрдЬрд╛рдпрд╛рдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдХрд░реНрдордкреНрд░рд╡рдЪрдиреАрдпрддреНрд╡рдореН ред ‘рд╕реНрд╡рддреА рдкреВрдЬрд╛рдпрд╛рдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рджрд┐рд╕рдорд╛рд╕рдГ, рддреЗрди рдЧрддрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рддреН ‘рд╕реВрдкрдорд╛рдирд╛рддреНрдХрдГ’ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрддреНрддрд░рдкрджрд╛рдиреНрддреЛрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рднрд╛рд╡реЗ рдЕрд╡реНрдпрдпрдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдкрджрдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд░рддреНрд╡рдореЗрд╡ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the great Indra, who is as a monarch the fulfiller (of the desires) of men, come hither; may he who is mighty over the two (realms of space), uninjurable by (hostile) offers, increase (in capacity) for heroism in our presence; may he who is great (in body), eminent (in qualities), be honoured by the performers (of pious acts).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Great is IndraтАФmanful, filling the domains and doubly lofty,
undiminishing in his powers.
Inclined toward us, he has been strengthened for his heroic deed.
Wide and broad, he was well made by his makers.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The published translation should read тАЬmanfullyтАЭ with adverbial nс╣Ыv├бt.

On possible configurations of the terms connected by ut├б, see Klein DGRV I.341.

Grassmann derives amin├б- from тИЪam (тАШm├дchtig andringend, gewaltigтАЩ), but it must belong to тИЪm─л as thematic parallel to ├бminant-. See Oldenberg (ZDMG 55.323).

The phrase in d, s├║kс╣Ыtaс╕е kartс╣Ы╠Бbhir bh┼лt тАЬhe was well made by his makers,тАЭ is somewhat startling as a description of the great god Indra. Who are his makers? Is this a depiction of his original creation, or does it have a more narrow and current application? Because of the previous p─Бda, тАж v─Бvс╣Ыdhe v─лry─Б╠Аya тАЬhe has been strengthened for his heroic deed,тАЭ I am inclined towards the latter: the soma drinks and ritual activities and praise have made him the consummate heroic actor. The pl.

agent noun kart├бr- may refer to the soma drinks or to the priests who prepared and offered them to Indra. Because I think the reference is to the immediate past, I would slightly alter the tr. from тАЬwas well madeтАЭ to тАЬhas been well made.тАЭ

Griffith

GREAT, hero-like controlling men is Indra, unwasting in his powers, doubled in vastness.
He, turned to us, hath grown to hero vigour: broad, wide, he hath been decked by those who serve him.

Keith

Great is Indra, manfully controlling men,
Unfailing in strength, of double force;
Towards us for strength doth he wax;
Broad and wide hath he been adorned by the offerers.

English translation:

тАЬOur praise encourages Indra o munificence, the vast, quick-moving, undecaying, ever-youthful Indra, mighty with unsurpassable strength, who rapidly grows to greatness.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The Holy Place positioned just Indra for winning, him lofty and towering, unaging and youthful,
swollen with invincible strength, who in just a single day grew strong and not by halves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

┼Ы├бvas─Б ┼Ы┼л┼Ыuv─Б╠Бс╣Гsam тАЬswollen with strengthтАЭ is an etymological figure, though ┼Ы├бvas- has lost its tight connection to тИЪ┼Ы┼л тАШswellтАЩ. Both words are reused in this hymn: 6a ┼Ы├бviс╣гс╣нham тАж ┼Ы├бvaс╕е тАЬstrongest strengthтАЭ; 7b, 8b ┼Ы┼л┼Ыuv─Б╠Бс╣Гsam.

Jamison Brereton Notes

These two vss. show a penchant for synonymous pairs: 1d ur├║с╕е pс╣Ыth├║с╕е тАЬwide (and) broad,тАЭ 2b bс╣Ыh├бntam с╣Ыс╣гv├бm тАЬlofty (and) towering,тАЭ aj├бraс╣Г y├║v─Бnam тАЬunaging (and) youthful.тАЭ

Griffith

The bowl made Indra swift to gather booty, the High, the Lofty, Youthful, Undecaying,
Him who hath waxed by strength which none may conquer, and even at once grown to complete perfection.

Geldner

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬExtend towards us your long, active, and bountiful hands, (to bring us) food; be abot us, lowly-minded Indra, in battle, as a herdsman (tends) the herds of cattle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Broad are your forearms, ample your fists. Mete out full measures of fame in our direction.
Like a herdsman to his flocks of livestock, as household master, o
Indra, turn here to us in the contest.

Griffith

Stretch out those hands of thine, extend to us-ward thy wide capacious arms, and grant us glory.
Like as the household herdsman guards the cattle, so move thou round about us in the combat.

Geldner

Breit sind deine Arme, umfangreich die H├дnde. Uns teile die Ehren zu! Wie der Hirt zu seiner Viehherde, so wende dich uns zu als Gebieter in der Schlacht, o Indra!

Grassmann

Gebreitet sind die Arme, weit die H├дnde zu uns gewandt, verleih uns sch├╢ne G├╝ter; Wie zu den Heerden sich des Hauses Viehhirt, so wende, Indra, dich zu uns im Kampfe.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDesiring sustenance, we invoke you, the renowned Indra, on this occasion, the destroyer (of enemies), together with his powerful allies (the Maruts); as his ancient adorers have been, (may we be), exempt from blame, irreproachable, unharmed.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Striving for the prizes of victory here and now, we would summon him for you, the elusive Indra along with his able (men);
(might we be) irreproachable, blameless, and invulnerable, just as the ancient singers were.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Since ┼Ы─Бk├б-, so accented, is the adj. тАШableтАЩ, not a noun ┼Ы─Б╠Бka- abilityтАЩ, I supply тАШmenтАЩ on the basis of IV.17.11 ebh├нr nс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е тАж asya ┼Ы─Бka├нс╕е.

With p─Бda d I supply opt. sy─Бma. Cf. II.27.7 ├║pa sy─Бma puruv─л╠Бr─Б ├бriс╣гс╣н─Бс╕е, sim.

vs. 16; X.128.3 ├бriс╣гс╣н─Бс╕е sy─Бma tanv─Б╠Аsuv─л╠Бr─Бс╕е.

Griffith

Now, fain for strength, let us invite your Indra hither, who lieth hidden with his Heroes,-
Free from all blame, without reproach, uninjured, e’en as were those who sang, of old, his praises.

Geldner

Diesen euren Indra, der mit seinen Gehilfen auszieht, wollen wir jetzt hierher rufen, auf Gewinn ausgehend, so wie die fr├╝heren S├дnger gewesen sind, ohne Tadel, ohne Makel, unverletzlich.

Grassmann

Der sich verbarg mit seinen Helden, Indra, ihn rufen wir euch her nun Gut begehrend, Wie auch die fr├╝hern S├дnger ohne Tadel und ohne Anstoss waren, ungef├дhrdet.

рд╕ рд╣рд┐ рд╕ рдЦрд▓реБ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдзреГрддрд╡реНрд░рддрдГ рдзреГрддрдХрд░реНрдорд╛ ред рдзрдирджрд╛рдГ рд╕ рдПрд╡ рдзрдирдкреНрд░рджрдГ ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢рд╕реНрдп рдзрдирд╕реНрдпреЗрддреНрдпрд╛рдХрд╛рдЩреНрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдпрд╛рдореБрдкрд╕рд░реНрдЬрдиреАрднреВрддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдкрд┐ рдзрдирд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдгреЗ рд╡рд╛рдорд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╕реБрди рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╡рд╛рдорд╕реНрдп рд╡рдирдиреАрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╕реБрдирдГ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдард╕реНрдп ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд╕реБрдиреЛ рдзрдирд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореАрддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГред рд╕реЛрдорд╡реГрджреНрдзрдГ рд╕ рдПрд╡ рд╕реЛрдореЗрди рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрджреНрдзрдГ ред рдкреБрд░реБрдХреНрд╖реБрдГ рдмрд╣реНрд╡рдиреНрдирдГ рд╕ рдПрд╡ ред рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░реЗ рдПрд╡ рдкрдереНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреДрдгрд╛рдВ рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐ рд░рд╛рдпрдГ рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ рд╕рдВ рдЬрдЧреНрдорд┐рд░реЗ рд╕рдВрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреЗ ред рддрддреНрд░ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдГ ред рд╕рд┐рдиреНрдзрд╡рдГ рдирджреНрдпрдГ рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░реЗ рди рдпрдерд╛ рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░реЗ рдпрд╛рджрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рдЕрднрд┐рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреНрдпрд╕реНрддрджреНрд╡рддреН рее рее рен рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIn him who is observant of pious rites, who is a giver of wealth, who is exalted by the Soma, the (lord) of desirable riches, the distributor of food, (in him) the treasures fit (for his worshippers) congregate like rivers flowing into ocean.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Of steadfast commandment, giving spoils, strengthened by soma (is he), for he is the possessor of much livestock, of goods worth winning.
The paths of wealth have joined in him, like the rivers uniting in the sea.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The gen. phrase v─Бm├бsya v├бsunaс╕е in b is difficult to construe. Geldner supplies тАЬ(Spender)тАЭ as its head noun; my tr. assumes that it is a loose genitive specification of the pa┼Ы├║- that is lurking in the -kс╣г├║- in the bahuvr─лhi puru-kс╣г├║- тАШpossessing much livestockтАЩ. This interpr. is suggested by the other occurrence of this gen. phrase in VIII.1.31 ut├б v─Бm├бsya v├бsuna┼Ы ciketati, y├│ ├бsti y─Б╠Бdvaс╕е pa┼Ы├║с╕е тАЬof the valuable goods what will stand out is the livestock coming from Yadu,тАЭ where the v─Бm├б- v├бsu- is identified as a particular pa┼Ы├║-. But the syntax proposed for our passage is sketchy.

By accent r─Б╠Бyaс╕е should be nom. pl., not, as I have tr. it, gen. sg. As Geldner suggests in his n. 5c, it reads literally тАЬthe paths, the riches тАжтАЭ Nonetheless, Oldenberg (ZDMG 55.324 and Noten) considers the nom. pl. reading тАЬforcedтАЭ (gezwungen) and interprets it as a gen. sg. (on the basis in part of VII.18.3 pathy─Б╠Аr─Бy├бс╕е with a clear gen. sg.). In the ZDMG treatment he explicitly says that emending the accent isnтАЩt necessary, though he doesnтАЩt indicate why.

In d Geldner suggests a haplology of *samudr├йс╣Зa n├б, with an instr. rather than a loc., as in III.36.7 samudr├йс╣Зa s├нndhavo y─Б╠Бdam─Бn─Бс╕е, where he proposes a similar haplology. This is possible, but not nec.: I see no reason why rivers canтАЩt unite in the sea as well as with it. As for III.36.7 see comm. ad loc.; I do not think that a simile particle is necessary there.

Griffith

With steadfast laws, wealth-giver, strong through Soma, he hath much fair and precious food to feed us.
In him unite all paths that lead to riches, like rivers that commingle with the ocean.

Geldner

Seine Gebote aufrecht haltend, Sch├дtze spendend, somagest├дrkt - denn der Viehbesitzer ist Spender sch├╢nen Gutes - in ihm laufen die Wege des Reichtums zusammen wie die Fl├╝sse, die sich mit dem Ozean vereinigen.

Grassmann

Gest├дrkt durch Soma, ist er Rechtsbeschirmer und Gutverleiher, sch├╢nen Schatzes Spender; Zu ihm hin gehen alle Reichthumspfade, wie zu dem Meere hin die Str├╢me eilen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBestow upon us, hero Indra, most vigorous vigour; subduer (of enemies, bestow upon us) most energetic and fierce energy; grant, lord of steeds, all the bright and invigorating (treasures) fit for men, to make us happy.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Bring here to us, o overpowering champion, the strongest strength, the mightiest mighty might.
All things brilliant and bullish that belong to the sons of ManuтАФgive them to us, o master of the fallow bays, to exhilarate us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich is notable for the superlative etymological figures: double ┼Ы├бviс╣гс╣нham тАж ┼Ы├бvaс╕е тАЬstrongest strengthтАЭ (or, in fact, triple, since ┼Ы┼лra тАШheroтАЩ is ultimately related to these words) and triple ├│jiс╣гс╣нham ├│jaс╕е тАж ugr├бm тАЬmightiest mighty might.тАЭ The triple etym. connection of the first phrase is better conveyed by GeldnerтАЩs тАЬBring uns, du Starker, die st├дrkste St├дrkeтАЭ than by the published translation Note also that the adjacent words in b ├│jo abhibh┼лta тАЬтАж might, o overpowering one,тАЭ though not syntactically connected here, form a bahuvr─лhi modifying Indra in the preceding hymn, VI.18.1 abh├нbh┼лti-ojas- тАШof overpowering strengthтАЩ.

06-08 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, all three of these vss. contain the phrase тАЬbring here to usтАЭ: in 6a and 7b na ─Б╠Бbhara straddles the early caesura; in 8a ─Б╠Бno bhara opens the vs. Since vss. 6-8 are the middle vss. of this hymn, this repeated phrase might identify an omphalos, but if so it is quite a weak one. The vss. are not particular noteworthy for their content, and the enclosing vss. do not provide the usual frame structure.

Griffith

Bring unto us the mightiest might, O Hero, strong and most potent force, thou great Subduer!
All splendid vigorous powers of men vouchsafe us, Lord of Bay Steeds, that they may make us joyful.

рдкреГрддрдирд╛рд╖рд╛рдЯреН рд╢рддреНрд░реБрд╕реЗрдирд╛рдирд╛рдорднрд┐рднрд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЕрдореГрдзреНрд░рдГ рдЕрд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд┐рддрдГ рдпрдГ рдорджрдГ рд╣рд░реНрд╖рдГ рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреЗ рддреНрд╡рдпрд╛ рджреЗрдпрдГ рд╢реВрд╢реБрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрджреНрдзрдВ рддрдВ рдорджрдВ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдореН рдЖ рднрд░ рдЖрд╣рд░ ред рддреНрд╡реЛрддрд╛рдГ рддреНрд╡рдпрд╛ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрд╛рдГ рдЬрд┐рдЧреАрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдГ рдЬрд┐рддрд╡рдиреНрддреЛ рд╡рдпрдВ рддреЛрдХрд╕реНрдп рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рддрдирдпрд╕реНрдп рддрддреНрдкреБрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдЪ рд╕рд╛рддреМ рд▓рд╛рднреЗ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрднреВрддреЗ рд╕рддрд┐ рдпреЗрди рд╣рд░реНрд╖реЗрдг рдордВрд╕реАрдорд╣рд┐ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрд╡реАрдорд╣рд┐ рддрдорд╛ рднрд░реЗрддрд┐ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЗрдгрд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬImpart to us, Indra, that your invigorating exultatio which overcomes enemies, and is irresistible, where by, protected by you, triumphant we may glorify you for the sake of (obtaining) sons and grandsons.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Your exhilaration, conquering in battle, never shirkingтАФbring us that, swollen with strength, o Indra,
through which we could be considered victors in the winning of
progeny and posterity, aided by you.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the long root vowel in jig─лv─Б╠Бс╣Гsaс╕е, see Oldenberg ZDMG 55.324, where on the basis of the metrical evidence he surmises that, at least in this post-caesura position, the form should be read with short root vowel (*jigi-vaс╣Гs-), the form found in the younger Vedic texts. See also Arnold (Ved. Met. 143), who considers the short-i form required in 3 of the 5 occurrences of the strong stem, and K├╝mmel (189 n. 225), who considers it proper except in III.15.4. K├╝mmel cites Anttila (1969, Schwebeabl. 61) as explaining the lengthening in the Saс╣Гhit─Б text as analogy to nin─лv─Б╠Бс╣Гs-. However, it is much more likely that it is a morphologically conditioned lengthening, meant to distinguish the -i-vowel proper to the root from the -i-liaison vowel that has become associated with suffixes/endings. Thus jig─л-v─Б╠Бс╣Гs- with long vowel is kept separate from the type tasth-iv─Б╠Бс╣Гs-, as I already argued in my 1988 article on the vocalized laryngeal (224-25), though without factoring in the metrical evidence pointing to this lengthening as late and redactional. (Of course, in tasthiv─Б╠Бс╣Гs- the -i- would originally have represented the zero-grade of this -─Б root, but by synchronic RV it has been reanalyzed as part of the suffix. See disc. in my 1988 art.)

Jamison Brereton Notes

I tr. ┼Ы┼л┼Ыuv─Б╠Бс╣Гsam in both vss. as тАШswollen with strengthтАЩ, although the ┼Ы├бvas─Б found in 2c is absent, as a portmanteau tr. to capture the full sense of the root.

This participle picks up ┼Ы├бviс╣гс╣нham тАж ┼Ы├бvaс╕е in vs. 6.

06-08 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, all three of these vss. contain the phrase тАЬbring here to usтАЭ: in 6a and 7b na ─Б╠Бbhara straddles the early caesura; in 8a ─Б╠Бno bhara opens the vs. Since vss. 6-8 are the middle vss. of this hymn, this repeated phrase might identify an omphalos, but if so it is quite a weak one. The vss. are not particular noteworthy for their content, and the enclosing vss. do not provide the usual frame structure.

Griffith

Bring us, grown mighty in its strength, O Indra, thy friendly rapturous joy that wins the battle,
Wherewith by thee assisted and triumphant, we may laud thee in gaining seed and offspring.

Geldner

Deinen Rausch, den Schlachtengewinner, den nicht geringen, den bring uns, Indra, mit, den starken, durch den wir glauben d├╝rfen bei dem Gewinnen von leiblichem Samen die von dir beg├╝nstigten Sieger zu sein.

Grassmann

Welch Muth dir ist, nicht rastend, Schlacht gewinnend, den bring uns her, o Indra, den gewalt’gen, Durch den erlangend Kinderschar und Enkel, von dir gef├╢rdert, siegreich wir uns zeigen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBestow upon us, Indra, vigorous strenght, the realizer of wealth, great and propitious, wherewith, thorugh your protection, we may destroy our enemies in battles, whether they be kinsmen or strangers.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Bring here to us, Indra, the bullish unbridled force that gains the stakes, swollen with strength, of good skill,
through which we will vanquish our rivals in battles, both kin and
non-kin, with your help.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In d the ut├б is oddly positioned, since it appears to be meant to conjoin j─Бm─л╠Бm╠Рr ├бj─Бm─лn тАЬkin and non-kin,тАЭ there being no other likely candidates. Klein (DGRV I.356-57) calls it a тАЬpeculiar passageтАЭ and classes it with two other examples of what he schematizes as ut├б X Y (/ Z тАж). The pair j─Бm├н- ├бj─Бmi- is several times asyndectic (I.111.3, IV.4.5, VI.44.17) as here, so no conjunction is actually necessary, but we can cite nearby VI.25.3 тАж j─Бm├бya ut├б y├й тАШj─Бmayaс╕е, where the ut├б is correctly placed. Perhaps our passage is a blend of the asyndectic figure and the тАЬX and which YтАЭ construction in VI.25.3.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, all three of these vss. contain the phrase тАЬbring here to usтАЭ: in 6a and 7b na ─Б╠Бbhara straddles the early caesura; in 8a ─Б╠Бno bhara opens the vs. Since vss. 6-8 are the middle vss. of this hymn, this repeated phrase might identify an omphalos, but if so it is quite a weak one. The vss. are not particular noteworthy for their content, and the enclosing vss. do not provide the usual frame structure.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay your invigorating srength come from the west, from the north, from the south, from the east; may it come to us from every quarter; grant us riches combined with felicity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let your unbridled force, a bull, come here from behind, here from above and below, here from in front.
Let it come altogether toward us from all sides. Indra, grant to us
sun-like brilliance.

Griffith

Let thine heroic strength come from behind us, before us, from above us or below us.
From every side may it approach us, Indra. Give us the glory of the realm of splendour.

Geldner

Dieser dein Mut komme wie ein Stier von hinten, von oben, von unten, von vorne, von allen Seiten soll er herkommen. O Indra, verleih uns sonnenhaften Glanz!

Grassmann

Her komme deine Heldenkraft von oben, von unten her, von vorne und von hinten, Von allen Seiten komme nah herbei sie, o Indra, schenk uns glanzbegabten Reichthum.

Elizarenkova

рдиреГрд╡рддреН рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреИрдГ рдкрд░рд┐рдЪрд╛рд░рдХрдЬрдиреИрд░реНрдпреБрдХреНрддрдВ рд╢реНрд░реЛрдорддреЗрднрд┐рдГ рд╢реНрд░реЛрддрд╡реНрдпреИрд░реНрдпрд╢реЛрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╣рд┐рддрдВ рд╡рд╛рдордВ рд╡рдирдиреАрдпрдВ рдзрдирдВ рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреЗ рддреНрд╡рддреНрддрдГ рдиреГрддрдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдиреЗрддреГрддрдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдКрддреА рдКрддрд┐рднреА рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛рднрд┐рдГ рд╡рдВрд╕реАрдорд╣рд┐ рд╡рдпрдВ рд╕рдВрднрдЬреЗрдорд╣рд┐ ред рд╣рд┐ рдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рдХрд╛рд░рдгрд╛рддреН рд╣реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреН рд░рд╛рдЬрдорд╛рдиреЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреНрд╡рдореН рдЙрднрдпрд╕реНрдп рдкрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рд╡рд╕реНрдп рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдЪ рд╡рд╕реНрд╡рдГ рдзрдирд╕реНрдп рдИрдХреНрд╖реЗ рдИрд╢рд┐рд╖реЗ рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рдХрд╛рд░рдгрд╛рддреН рдорд╣рд┐ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рд╕реНрдереВрд░рдВ рд╡рд┐рдкреБрд▓рдВ рдмреГрд╣рдиреНрддрдВ рдЧреБрдгреИрдГ рдкрд░рд┐рд╡реГрдврдВ рд░рддреНрдирдВ рд░рдордгреАрдпрдВ рдзрдирдореН ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд░рддреНрдирд╢рдмреНрджрдГ рдкреБрд▓реНрд▓рд┐рдБрдЩреНрдЧрдГ ред рдзрд╛рдГ рдзреЗрд╣рд┐ рее

English translation:

тАЬWe enjoy, Indra, through your guiding protection, desirable affluence along with descendants and reputation; grant us, sovereign, who rule over (earthly and heavenly) riches, vast, desirable and infinite treasures.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Manfully, with your most manly help, Indra, we would win what is worth winning through your attentions.
Because you are master of both kinds of good, o king, grant a great, substantial, lofty treasure.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The medial 1st pl. s-aor. opt. vaс╣Гs─лm├бhi contrasts with the active 1st pl. saor. subjunctive v├бс╣Гs─Бma in 8c, but the medial optative must have been modeled on the rhyme form maс╣Гs─лm├бhi in the same metrical position in 7d. The тАЬrestтАЭ following vaс╣Гs─лm├бhi may call attention to the verb by isolating it metrically.

Besides this echo, note also nс╣Ыv├бt, which replicates nс╣Ыv├бt in 1a, and v─Бm├бm recalling v─Бm├бsya in 5b, while the gen. v├бsvaс╕е is in slight discord with the differently formed gen. v├бsunaс╕е in 5b.

I tr. ┼Ыr├│matebhiс╕е as тАШattentionsтАЩ, that is, the attentive hearing(s) that Indra gives to menтАЩs words. For similar use of ┼Ыr├│mata- in a somewhat clearer context see VII.40.5.

The referent of the тАЬboth kinds of good[s]тАЭ in c is not clear, at least from immediate context. In the very similar passage VII.82.4 ─л┼Ы─Бn─Б╠Бv├бsva ubh├бyasya, it seems to refer to goods belonging to war and peace; similarly in the next hymn, VII.83.5 yuv├бс╣Г h├н v├бsva ubh├бyasya r─Б╠Бjathaс╕е, where a reference to war and peace – or perhaps to the goods of enemies and of allies – is likely. In II.9.5 the referent of ubh├бyam тАж vasavy├аm is also open-ended, but RenouтАЩs suggestion there that itтАЩs livestock and offspring is perhaps the most satisfactory. In our passage the nearest contrastive pair is j─Бm─л╠Бm╠Рr ├бj─Бm─лn тАЬkin and non-kinтАЭ in 8c, so perhaps тАЬboth kinds of good[s]тАЭ refers to the goods belonging to these two groups whom we hope vanquish in battle. Note vс╣Ыtr─Б╠Бс╣Зy ubh├бy─Бni тАЬboth kinds of obstaclesтАЭ in 13c, which Geldner, persuasively, takes as referring to the тАЬkin and non-kinтАЭ of 8d. Michael Weiss suggests another possibility: тАЬmovable and immovable,тАЭ which has a fine Indo-European pedigree.

The acc. obj. phrase in d, r├бtnam m├бhi sth┼лr├бm bс╣Ыh├бntam, contains an apparent gender clash: r├бtna- is neut., as is m├бhi; sth┼лr├бm can be either neut. or masc., while bс╣Ыh├бntam must be masc. It is tempting to correlate the two genders with the two kinds of goods in p─Бda c: a тАЬgreat treasureтАЭ (neut.) and тАЬsubstantial lofty XтАЭ (masc.). This might be possible: sth┼лr├б- bс╣Ыh├бnt- qualifies masc. ray├н- in IV.21.4 sth┼лr├бsya r─Бy├│ bс╣Ыhat├│ y├б ─л╠Б┼Ыe (and cf. X.156.3 ─Б╠Бgne sth┼лr├бс╣Г ray├нm bhara), and bс╣Ыh├бnt- not infrequently modifies ray├н- (cf., e.g., VI.6.7). Thus, we could assume an underlying *ray├нm for the last two adjectives, yielding a tr. тАЬgrant a great treasure (and) substantial lofty (wealth).тАЭ This might be supported by r─Бy─Б╠БтАж bс╣Ыhat─Б╠Бin the last p─Бda of the hymn (13d). Nonetheless, this seems unduly artificial, and I would prefer to assume that at the end of this acc. phrase, encouraged by ambig. sth┼лr├бm, bс╣Ыh├бntam has simply taken its accustomed p─Бda-final place in Triс╣гс╣нubh. As reported by Oldenberg (ZDMG 55.325 and Noten), Ludwig suggested substituting (that is, emending) ray├нm for m├бhi, a suggestion roundly rejected by Oldenberg, who simply says (Noten) that masc. bс╣Ыh├бntam is construed with neut. r├бtnam.

Griffith

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe invoke on this occasion for his present protection, that Indra who is attended by the Maruts; who is the showerer (of benefits); augmenting (in prowess); the unreviled of foes, radiant, ruling, all-subduing, fierce, the giver of strength.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Him, accompanied by the Maruts, the bull grown strong, not stingy, the heavenly commanderтАФIndraтАФ
the all-conquering, mighty giver of strengthтАФhim we would invoke here for present help.

Griffith

The Bull, whose strength hath waxed, whom Maruts follow, free-giving Indra, the Celestial Ruler,
Mighty, all-conquering, the victory-giver, him let us call to grant us new protection.

Geldner

Den erstarkten Bullen in Begleitung der Marutschar, der kein geiziger Herr ist, den himmlischen Gebieter Indra, den Allbezwinger, den gewaltigen Siegverleiher, den wollen wir zu erneutem Beistand hierher rufen.

Grassmann

Den Marutherrscher Indra, den erstarkten, der nimmer geizt, den himmlischen Gebieter, Den Allbesieger, starken Kraftverleiher, ihn rufen wir herbei zu neuer H├╝lfe.

Elizarenkova

рдпреЗрд╖реБ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдиреГрдгрд╛рдВ рдордзреНрдпреЗрд╜рд╣рдореН рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐ рдПрдХреЛ рднрд╡рд╛рдорд┐ рд╣реЗ рд╡рдЬреНрд░рд┐рдиреН рд╡рдЬреНрд░рд╡рдиреН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреНрд╡рдореН рдПрднреНрдпреЛ рдиреГрднреНрдп рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЗрднреНрдпрдГ рдорд╣рд┐ рдорд╣рджрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдирдВ рдордиреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдВ рдЬрдирдореН ред рдмрд╣реБрдордиреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рд░рдиреНрдзрдп рд╡рд╢реАрдХреБрд░реБ рдЪрд┐рддреН рдЗрддрд┐ рдкрд╛рджрдкреВрд░рдгрдГ ред рдЕрдз рдЕрдзреБрдирд╛ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдВ рднреВрдореНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╢реВрд░рд╕рд╛рддреМ рдпреБрджреНрдзреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрддреНрддреЗ рд╕рддрд┐ рддрдирдпреЗ рдкреБрддреНрд░реЗ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрдВ рдЪ рдЧреЛрд╖реБ рдкрд╢реБрд╖реБ рдЕрдкреНрд╕реБ рдЙрджрдХреЗрд╖реБ рдЪ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддреЗрд╖реБ рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреНрд╡рд╛ рджреНрдпреБрд▓реЛрдХреЗ рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рд╣рд╡рд╛рдорд╣реЗ рд╡рдпрдорд╛рд╣реНрд╡рдпрд╛рдордГ ред

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWielder of the thunderbolt, humble that man who looks upon himself as the greatest among those men of whom I am; we invoke you now to (ascend) upon the earth at the time of battle, and for (the sake of obtaining) sond and grandsons.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The person who thinks himself to be ever so great, o mace-bearerтАФ make him subject to these superior men, among whom am IтАФ
for therefore do we summon you at the contest of champions when the earth, lineage, cows, and waters (are at stake).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note a different kind of gender mismatch in p─Бda a. Though in the idiom with тИЪman тАЬconsider oneself XтАЭ / тАЬbe considered as X,тАЭ X is in the same case as the underlying subject (see, e.g., 7c maс╣Гs─лmahi jig─лv─Бс╣Гsaс╕е тАЬwe could be considered victorsтАЭ), here it is construed with an adverbial neut. m├бhi. That this is not necessarily a property of тАЬthink oneself greatтАЭ is shown by I.178.5, VII.98.4 mahat├│ m├бnyam─Бn─Бn тАЬтАж those thinking themselves great,тАЭ with acc. pl. matching the subject of the participle.

Griffith

Give up the people who are high and haughty to these men and to me, O Thunder-wielder!
Therefore upon the earth do we invoke thee, where heroes win, for sons and kine and waters.

Geldner

Jedermann, mag er noch so gro├Я sich d├╝nken, mach, du Keulentr├дger, diesen Herrn untertan, auf deren Seite ich bin; denn darum rufen wir dich im Kampf um Land, um den tapfersten Helden, um leibliche Kinder, um Rinder, um Wasser.

Grassmann

Den Mann, der gross sich d├╝nkt, den ├╝berliefre den M├дnnern, Blitzesherr, bei denen ich bin; Denn in dem Kampfe jetzt im Lande rufen wir dich um Kinder, K├╝he an und Wasser.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬInvoked of many, may we, through these your friendly (praises), ever be superior to successive foes, destroying, oс╕е hero, both (classes of) enemies, (kindred or unallied); and may we, protected by you, be happy with abundant riches.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

By these partnerships with you, o much invoked one, might we be higher than each and every rival.
Smashing both kinds of obstacles, o champion, we would be exultant through lofty wealth, when helped by you.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On vс╣Ыtr─Б╠Бс╣Зy ubh├бy─Бni тАЬboth kinds of obstaclesтАЭ see comm. ad vs. 10.

Griffith

Through these thy friendships, God invoked of many! may we be victors over every foeman.
Slaying both kinds of foe, may we, O Hero, be happy, helped by thee, with ample riches.

Geldner

Wir wollen durch diese deine Freundschaftdienste, Vielgerufener, ├╝ber jeden Feind die Oberhand haben. Beiderlei Feinde schlagend, o Held, wollen wir von dir beg├╝nstigt in gro├Яem Reichtum schwelgen.

Grassmann

Durch diese deine Freundschaft, vielgerufner, lass Sieger sein uns ├╝ber alle Hasser, Die beiderseit’gen Feind’, o Held, erschlagend, durch deine Huld an grossem Gut uns labend.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рдЙрд╕реА рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рдкреБрд░реБрд╣реВрдд) рдмрд╣реБрддреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рдд (рд╢реВрд░) рд╡реАрд░ рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреН ! (рд╡рдпрдореН) рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ (рддреЗ) рдЖрдкрдХреЗ (рдПрднрд┐рдГ) рдЗрди рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди, рдкрд╣рд┐рд▓реЗ рдХрд╣реЗ рдЧрдпреЗ рдФрд░ рдЙрддреНрддрд░реЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрд╛рджрд┐рдд (рд╕рдЦреНрдпреИрдГ) рдорд┐рддреНрд░ рдХреЗ рдХрд░реНрдореЛрдВ рд╕реЗ (рд╢рддреНрд░реЛрдГрд╢рддреНрд░реЛрдГ) рд╢рддреНрд░реБ-рд╢рддреНрд░реБ рдХреА рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдУрдВ рдХрд╛ (рдШреНрдирдиреНрддрдГ) рдирд╛рд╢ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП (рдЙрддреНрддрд░реЗ) рд╡рд┐рдЬрдп рдХреЗ рдЕрдирдиреНрддрд░ рд╕рдордп рдореЗрдВ (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) рдкреНрд░рдХрдЯ рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ рдФрд░ (рдЙрднрдпрд╛рдирд┐) рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдФрд░ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрди рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди (рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐) рдзрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рдЖрдкрдХреА (рдмреГрд╣рддрд╛) рдмреЬреА (рд░рд╛рдпрд╛) рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдореА рд╕реЗ рддрдерд╛ (рддреНрд╡реЛрддрд╛рдГ) рдЖрдк рд╕реЗ рдкрд╛рд▓рдирд╛ рдХрд┐рдпреЗ рд╣реБрдП (рдЗрддреН) рд╣реА (рдорджреЗрдо) рдЖрдирдиреНрдж рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ реерезрейрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдФрд░ рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрди рдорд┐рддреНрд░ рдХреЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢ рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ рддреЛ рд╕рдореНрдкреВрд░реНрдг рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреЛ рдЬреАрдд рдХрд░ рдмреЬреА рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдореА рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд┐рдд рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ реерезрейрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░, рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдФрд░ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдХреГрддреНрдп рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рдЙрдиреНрдиреАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдЖрдард╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдкреБрд░реБрд╣реВрдд рд╢реВрд░ рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреН ! рд╡рдпрдВ рдд рдПрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рдЦреНрдпреИрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реЛрдГрд╢рддреНрд░реЛрдГ рд╕реЗрдирд╛ рдШреНрдирдиреНрдд рдЙрддреНрддрд░реЗ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдореЛрднрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рд▓рдмреНрдзреНрд╡рд╛ рддрд╡ рдмреГрд╣рддрд╛ рд░рд╛рдпрд╛ рддреНрд╡реЛрддрд╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрдд рдЗрдиреНрдорджреЗрдо реерезрейрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╡рдпрдореН) (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рдПрднрд┐рдГ) рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдиреИрдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛрдХреНрддреИрд░реБрддреНрддрд░рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрд╛рджрд┐рддреИрдГ (рдкреБрд░реБрд╣реВрдд) рдмрд╣реБрднрд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рдд (рд╕рдЦреНрдпреИрдГ) рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдХрд░реНрдорднрд┐рдГ (рд╢рддреНрд░реЛрдГрд╢рддреНрд░реЛрдГ) (рдЙрддреНрддрд░реЗ) рд╡рд┐рдЬрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрддрд░рд╕рдордпреЗ (рдЗрддреН) рдПрд╡ (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) (рдШреНрдирдиреНрддрдГ) (рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐) рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ (рдЙрднрдпрд╛рдирд┐) рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд┐ (рд╢реВрд░) (рд░рд╛рдпрд╛) рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╢реНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛ (рдорджреЗрдо) рдЖрдирдиреНрджреЗрдо (рдмреГрд╣рддрд╛) рдорд╣рддрд╛ (рддреНрд╡реЛрддрд╛рдГ) рддреНрд╡рдпрд╛ рдкрд╛рд▓рд┐рддрд╛рдГ реерезрейрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрджрд┐ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдирд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рд╕реБрд╣реГрджреНрд╡рддреН рд╕реНрдпреБрд╕реНрддрд░реНрд╣рд┐ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдЮреНрдЫрддреНрд░реВрдиреН рд╡рд┐рдЬрд┐рддреНрдп рдорд╣рддреНрдпрд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╢реНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗрд░рдиреНрдирд┐рддрд┐ реерезрейрее рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдирдХреГрддреНрдпрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХреЛрдирд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдорд╖реНрдЯрдореЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬрд░ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рд╡ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгреЗ рд╡рд╛рдЧрд▓реЗ рддрд░ рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдВрдирд╛ рдЬрд┐рдВрдХреВрди рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдореА рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ. рее резрей рее
